838

839 <section id="_1004">

840

841 <h2>

842Executive Summary</h2>

843

844 <div id="_section_1004" class="pdq-sections">

845<p id="_1005" tabindex="-1">

846This executive summary reviews the topics covered in this PDQ summary on cancer genetics risk assessment and genetic counseling, with hyperlinks to detailed sections below that describe the evidence on each topic.</p>

847<div class="pdq-content-list">

848<ul id="_1006">

849<li>

850<strong>

851Identification of Individuals for Cancer Genetics Risk Assessment and Counseling</strong>

852<p id="_1007" tabindex="-1">

853Individuals are considered to be candidates for cancer risk assessment if they have a personal and/or family history (on the maternal or paternal side) or clinical characteristics with <a href="/about-cancer/causes-prevention/genetics/risk-assessment-pdq#_7">

854features suggestive of hereditary cancer</a>

855. These features vary by type of cancer and specific hereditary syndrome. Criteria have been published to help identify individuals who may benefit from genetic counseling. It is important that individuals who are candidates for genetic testing undergo genetic education and counseling before testing to facilitate informed decision-making and adaptation to the risk or condition. <a href="/about-cancer/causes-prevention/genetics/risk-assessment-pdq#_322">

856Genetic education and counseling</a>

857 allow individuals to understand the risks, benefits, and limitations of genetic testing. This also allows individuals to consider possible medical uncertainties, cancer diagnoses, and/or medical management plans that accompany certain genetic test results.</p>

858</li>

859<li>

860<strong>

861Components of Cancer Genetics Risk Assessment and Counseling</strong>

862<p id="_1504" tabindex="-1">

863Comprehensive <a href="/about-cancer/causes-prevention/genetics/risk-assessment-pdq#_142">

864cancer risk assessment and counseling</a>

865 is a consultative service that includes clinical assessment, genetic testing when appropriate, and risk management recommendations delivered in the context of one or more genetic counseling sessions. Pretest genetic counseling is an important part of the risk assessment process and helps patients understand their genetic testing options and potential outcomes. Posttest genetic counseling helps patients understand their test results, including the medical implications for themselves and their relatives.</p>

866<p id="_1505" tabindex="-1">

867The recommended provision of cancer risk assessment services optimally involves care providers from multiple disciplines, including a genetic counselor; a genetics advanced practice nurse; a medical geneticist or a physician, such as an oncologist, surgeon, or internist; and potential referrals to other specialists, such as mental health professionals, endocrinologists, and reproductive specialists.</p>

868<p id="_1506" tabindex="-1">

869Traditionally, <a href="/about-cancer/causes-prevention/genetics/risk-assessment-pdq#_1489">

870genetic counseling services</a>

871 have been delivered using individualized, in-person appointments. However, other methodologies are being increasingly utilized, including group sessions, telephone counseling, and telemedicine by videoconferencing.</p>

872</li>

873<li>

874<strong>

875Genetic Testing Considerations</strong>

876<p id="_1010" tabindex="-1">

877There are many <a href="/about-cancer/causes-prevention/genetics/risk-assessment-pdq#_78">

878factors that can influence an individual&#8217;s decision to undergo genetic testing</a>

879 and which type of test to use, including the presence of a <a href="/about-cancer/causes-prevention/genetics/risk-assessment-pdq#_307">

880known pathogenic variant in the family</a>

881, patterns of cancer in the family, <a href="/about-cancer/causes-prevention/genetics/risk-assessment-pdq#_1464">

882insurance coverage</a>

883, <a href="/about-cancer/causes-prevention/genetics/risk-assessment-pdq#_318">

884family planning considerations</a>

885, and the psychological impact of a test result. Previously, most germline genetic testing was offered for a single gene at a time; however, recent technological advances have resulted in the widespread availability of <a href="/about-cancer/causes-prevention/genetics/risk-assessment-pdq#_1320">

886multigene (panel) testing</a>

887, which can simultaneously test for pathogenic variants in many genes at once, often at costs comparable to single-gene testing. <a href="/about-cancer/causes-prevention/genetics/risk-assessment-pdq#_1325">

888Research has examined the use and outcomes of multigene testing</a>

889. </p>

890<p id="_1867" tabindex="-1">

891Some health-related cancer genetic tests are also offered as <a href="/about-cancer/causes-prevention/genetics/risk-assessment-pdq#_362">

892direct-to-consumer (DTC) tests</a>

893. While these tests may promote access and patient autonomy, the process may not include genetic counseling or interpretation of the results by a genetics professional. In addition, these tests may be incomplete or require confirmation with a second DNA sample sent to another clinical laboratory.</p>

894<p id="_1816" tabindex="-1">

895<a href="/about-cancer/causes-prevention/genetics/risk-assessment-pdq#_1609">

896Cascade genetic testing</a>

897 can be effective in identifying carriers of a pathogenic variant prior to cancer presentation which provides opportunities for cancer prevention, early detection, risk reduction, and ultimately improved health outcomes.</p>

898<p id="_1817" tabindex="-1">

899Various <a href="/about-cancer/causes-prevention/genetics/risk-assessment-pdq#_1610">

900cancer genetic service delivery</a>

901 approaches are being used to facilitate greater access to genetic counseling and testing. These approaches have been utilized to streamline the process by which high-risk or affected individuals are identified and referred to specialty genetic services for additional evaluation. These service delivery models vary in the processes by which patients receive genetic education, counseling, and testing.</p>

902</li>

903<li>

904<strong>

905Ethical, Legal, and Social Implications</strong>

906<p id="_1012" tabindex="-1">

907Having an understanding of the <a href="/about-cancer/causes-prevention/genetics/risk-assessment-pdq#_240">

908ethical, legal, and social implications</a>

909 regarding cancer genetic testing may influence the clinician&#8217;s response to the complex questions and issues that may arise during the process of risk assessment and counseling. There are several ethical and legal considerations that factor into decisions about what responsibility, if any, providers have to directly inform at-risk relatives about hereditary cancer risks. This section addresses <a href="/about-cancer/causes-prevention/genetics/risk-assessment-pdq#_1738">

910duty to warn</a>

911, including legal frameworks and available guidance from professional societies. Consultation with an ethicist, ethics committee, legal counsel, privacy officer, and when applicable, an institutional review board, may be warranted in certain disclosure situations.</p>

912<p id="_1507" tabindex="-1">

913<a href="/about-cancer/causes-prevention/genetics/risk-assessment-pdq#_1787">

914Employment and insurance discrimination</a>

915 are common concerns for individuals considering genetic testing. The <a href="/about-cancer/causes-prevention/genetics/risk-assessment-pdq#_1792">

916Genetic Information Nondiscrimination Act of 2008 (GINA)</a>

917, a Federal law passed in 2008, protects against health insurance and employment discrimination on the basis of genetics information for most people; however, it does not apply to members of the military or to long-term care, disability, and life insurance provisions.</p>

918</li>

919</ul>

920</div>

921</div>

922

923 </section>

924

925

926

927 <section id="_5">

928

929 <h2>

930Introduction</h2>

931

932 <div id="_section_5" class="pdq-sections">

933<p id="_272" tabindex="-1">

934[<em>

935Note: Many of the medical and scientific terms used in this summary are found in the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/dictionaries/genetics-dictionary" title="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/dictionaries/genetics-dictionary">

936NCI Dictionary of Genetics Terms</a>

937. When a linked term is clicked, the definition will appear in a separate window.</em>

938]</p>

939<p id="_1466" tabindex="-1">

940[<em>

941Note: A concerted effort is being made within the genetics community to shift terminology used to describe genetic variation. The shift is to use the term &#8220;variant&#8221; rather than the term &#8220;mutation&#8221; to describe a difference that exists between the person or group being studied and the reference sequence, particularly for differences that exist in the germline. Variants can then be further classified as benign (harmless), likely benign, of uncertain significance, likely pathogenic, or pathogenic (disease causing). Throughout this summary, we will use the term pathogenic variant to describe a disease-causing mutation. For more information about variant classification, see <a href="/about-cancer/causes-prevention/genetics/overview-pdq#_2676">

942Cancer Genetics Overview</a>

943.</em>

944]</p>

945<p id="_6" tabindex="-1">

946This summary describes current approaches to assessing and

947counseling people about their chance of having an inherited susceptibility to

948cancer. <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44961&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=genetic" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044961&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=genetic'); return(false);">

949Genetic counseling</a>

950 is defined by the <a href="https://www.nsgc.org/page/faqs#counseling" title="https://www.nsgc.org/page/faqs#counseling">

951National Society of Genetic Counselors</a>

952 as the process of helping people understand and adapt to the medical, psychological, and familial implications of genetic contributions to disease. Several reviews present overviews of the cancer <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=460214&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=genetic" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000460214&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=genetic'); return(false);">

953risk assessment</a>

954, counseling, and genetic testing process.[<a href="#cit/section_2.1">

9551</a>

956,<a href="#cit/section_2.2">

9572</a>

958] </p>

959<p id="_319" tabindex="-1">

960Individuals are considered to be candidates for cancer risk assessment if they have personal and/or family histories (in maternal or paternal lineages) with features suggestive of hereditary cancer.[<a href="#cit/section_2.1">

9611</a>

962] These features vary by type of cancer and specific hereditary syndrome. Practice resources have been published to help clinicians identify individuals who may benefit from a genetics evaluation and/or genetic counseling. Organizations like the National Comprehensive Cancer Network frequently update related genetic counseling and genetic testing guidelines.[<a href="#cit/section_2.1">

9631</a>

964,<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

9653</a>

966-<a href="#cit/section_2.6">

9676</a>

968] The PDQ cancer genetics information summaries on <a href="/types/breast/hp/breast-ovarian-genetics-pdq">

969breast</a>

970, <a href="/types/breast/hp/breast-ovarian-genetics-pdq">

971ovarian</a>

972, <a href="/types/breast/hp/breast-ovarian-genetics-pdq">

973endometrial</a>

974, <a href="/types/colorectal/hp/colorectal-genetics-pdq">

975colorectal</a>

976, <a href="/types/prostate/hp/prostate-genetics-pdq">

977prostate</a>

978, <a href="/types/kidney/hp/renal-cell-carcinoma-genetics">

979kidney</a>

980, and <a href="/types/skin/hp/skin-genetics-pdq">

981skin</a>

982 cancers and <a href="/types/thyroid/hp/medullary-thyroid-genetics-pdq">

983endocrine and neuroendocrine neoplasias</a>

984 describe the clinical features of hereditary syndromes associated with these conditions.</p>

985<p id="_7" tabindex="-1">

986The following are features that suggest hereditary cancer:[<a href="#cit/section_2.7">

9877</a>

988-<a href="#cit/section_2.11">

98911</a>

990]</p>

991<div class="pdq-content-list">

992<ul id="_8">

993<li>

994Unusually early age of cancer onset (e.g., premenopausal breast cancer).</li>

995<li>

996Multiple primary cancers in a single individual (e.g., colorectal and endometrial cancer).</li>

997<li>

998Bilateral cancer in paired organs or multifocal disease (e.g., bilateral breast cancer or multifocal renal cancer).</li>

999<li>

1000Clustering of the same type of cancer in close relatives (e.g., mother, daughter, and sisters with breast cancer).</li>

1001<li>

1002Cancers occurring in multiple generations of a family (i.e., <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=793860&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=genetic" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000793860&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=genetic'); return(false);">

1003autosomal dominant inheritance</a>

1004).</li>

1005<li>

1006Occurrence of rare tumors (e.g., retinoblastoma, adrenocortical carcinoma, granulosa cell tumor of the ovary, ocular melanoma, or duodenal cancer).</li>

1007<li>

1008Occurrence of epithelial ovarian, fallopian tube, or primary peritoneal cancer.</li>

1009<li>

1010Unusual presentation of cancer (e.g., male breast cancer).</li>

1011<li>

1012Uncommon tumor histology (e.g., medullary thyroid carcinoma).</li>

1013<li>

1014Rare cancers associated with birth defects (e.g., Wilms tumor and genitourinary abnormalities).</li>

1015<li>

1016Geographic or ethnic populations known to be at high risk of hereditary cancers. Genetic testing candidates may be identified based solely on ethnicity when a strong <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=783962&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=genetic" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000783962&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=genetic'); return(false);">

1017founder effect</a>

1018 is present in a given population (e.g., <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=460127&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=genetic" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000460127&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=genetic'); return(false);">

1019Ashkenazi</a>

1020 heritage and <em class="gene-name">

1021BRCA1</em>

1022/<em class="gene-name">

1023BRCA2</em>

1024 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=783960&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=genetic" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000783960&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=genetic'); return(false);">

1025pathogenic variants</a>

1026).</li>

1027</ul>

1028</div>

1029<p id="_279" tabindex="-1">

1030As part of the process of genetic education and counseling, genetic testing may be considered when the following factors are present:[<a href="#cit/section_2.12">

103112</a>

1032-<a href="#cit/section_2.14">

103314</a>

1034]</p>

1035<div class="pdq-content-list">

1036<ul id="_280">

1037<li>

1038An individual's personal history (including ethnicity) and/or family history are suspicious for a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=460153&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=genetic" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000460153&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=genetic'); return(false);">

1039genetic predisposition</a>

1040 to cancer.</li>

1041<li>

1042The genetic test has sufficient <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=322883&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=genetic" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000322883&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=genetic'); return(false);">

1043sensitivity</a>

1044 and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=322884&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=genetic" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000322884&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=genetic'); return(false);">

1045specificity</a>

1046 to be interpreted.</li>

1047<li>

1048The test will impact the individual's diagnosis, cancer management or cancer risk management, and/or help clarify risk in family members.</li>

1049</ul>

1050</div>

1051<p id="_9" tabindex="-1">

1052It is important that genetic testing candidates undergo genetic education and counseling prior to testing. This process allows greater understanding of disease risk and helps facilitate informed decision making.[<a href="#cit/section_2.1">

10531</a>

1054,<a href="#cit/section_2.10">

105510</a>

1056-<a href="#cit/section_2.16">

105716</a>

1058] Genetic education and counseling allow individuals to understand the risks, benefits, and limitations of genetic testing. This also allows individuals to consider possible medical uncertainties, cancer diagnoses, and/or medical management plans that accompany certain genetic test results.</p>

1133 <section id="_1458">

1134

1135 <h2>

1136Identification of Candidates for Referral to Genetic Counseling</h2>

1137

1138 <div id="_section_1458" class="pdq-sections">

1139<nav class="in-this-section" role="navigation">

1140<h6>

1141In This Section</h6>

1142<ul>

1143<li>

1144<a href="#_1459_toc">

1145Tools to Identify Candidates for Genetic Counseling and Genetic Testing</a>

1146</li>

1147</ul>

1148</nav>

1149<p id="_1353" tabindex="-1">

1150After an individual&#8217;s personal and family cancer histories have been collected, several factors could warrant referral to a genetics professional for evaluation of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=754220&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=genetic" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000754220&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=genetic'); return(false);">

1151hereditary cancer syndromes</a>

1152. The American College of Medical Genetics and Genomics (ACMG) and the National Society of Genetic Counselors (NSGC) have published a <a href="https://www.nature.com/articles/gim2014147#recommendations" title="https://www.nature.com/articles/gim2014147#recommendations">

1153comprehensive set of personal and family history criteria</a>

1154 to guide the identification of at-risk individuals and appropriate referral for cancer genetic risk consultation.[<a href="#cit/section_3.1">

11551</a>

1156] These practice guidelines address tumor types, other potential features, and related criteria that would prompt a genetics referral. ACMG and NSGC state that the guidelines are intended to maximize appropriate referral of at-risk individuals for cancer genetics consultations, but they are not meant to provide genetic testing or treatment recommendations. Furthermore, ACMG and NSGC acknowledge other sources that provide updated and evolving genetic testing criteria (e.g., the National Comprehensive Cancer Network [NCCN]) and the increasing role of nongenetics professionals in facilitating genetic testing, especially to guide cancer treatment.[<a href="#cit/section_3.2">

11572</a>

1158] For more information, see the <a href="/about-cancer/causes-prevention/genetics/risk-assessment-pdq#_1610">

1159Cancer Genetics Service Delivery</a>

1160 section.</p>

1161<section id="_1459">

1162<h3 id="_1459_toc">

1163Tools to Identify Candidates for Genetic Counseling and Genetic Testing</h3>

1164<p id="_1508" tabindex="-1">

1165All major societies recommend genetic services for patients at a moderate or high risk of having a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=754220&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=genetic" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000754220&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=genetic'); return(false);">

1166hereditary cancer syndrome</a>

1167. In addition to published guidelines available through professional organizations,[<a href="#cit/section_3.2">

11682</a>

1169-<a href="#cit/section_3.5">

11705</a>

1171] there are also red flag cards, paper-based checklists, chatbots, and patient-directed online referral tools to identify patients who are candidates for genetic counseling and genetic testing. There are a number of commercially available tools (not addressed in this summary) that also offer risk assessment and/or facilitate genetic evaluation. These brief and simple screening tools may be administered to patients in a provider's waiting room or online prior to a visit. Some tools are publicly available and can be accessed directly by patients. For a list of some of these tools, see <a href="/about-cancer/causes-prevention/genetics/overview-pdq#_76">

1172the table on Risk Assessment Information</a>

1173 and <a href="/about-cancer/causes-prevention/genetics/overview-pdq#_77">

1174the table on Online Pathogenic Variant Prediction Programs </a>

1175 in Cancer Genetics Overview.</p>

1176<p id="_1926" tabindex="-1">

1177Many of these tools assess common features suggestive of hereditary cancer, but there are limitations. For example, there is variability in the tools' abilities to flag at-risk individuals based on extensive criteria, as outlined by current professional society guidelines (e.g., NCCN). Hence, some people who are candidates for genetic counseling and genetic testing will be missed by these tools. This includes individuals who may be considered low-risk based on these screening tools. Because of the potential clinical utility of genetic testing, clinical judgement may still be needed to determine the appropriateness of genetic counseling and testing in these individuals. Thus, clinical review of information on screening forms is still warranted.</p>

1178<p id="_1879" tabindex="-1">

1179Additional tools are available to assess the risk of harboring a specific pathogenic variant in a cancer susceptibility gene. For more information, see the <a href="/types/breast/hp/breast-ovarian-genetics-pdq#_66">

1180Models for Prediction of Breast and Gynecologic Cancer Risk</a>

1181 section in Genetics of Breast and Gynecologic Cancers and the <a href="/types/colorectal/hp/colorectal-genetics-pdq#_1101">

1182Clinical risk assessment models that predict the likelihood of an MMR gene pathogenic variant</a>

1183 section in Genetics of Colorectal Cancer.</p>

1184</section>

1215 <section id="_142">

1216

1217 <h2>

1218Cancer Risk Assessment and Counseling</h2>

1219

1220 <div id="_section_142" class="pdq-sections">

1221<nav class="in-this-section" role="navigation">

1222<h6>

1223In This Section</h6>

1224<ul>

1225<li>

1226<a href="#_322_toc">

1227Genetic Counseling</a>

1228</li>

1229<li>

1230<a href="#_323_toc">

1231Pretest Genetic Education and Counseling Outcomes</a>

1232</li>

1233</ul>

1234</nav>

1235<p id="_320" tabindex="-1">

1236Comprehensive cancer <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=460214&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=genetic" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000460214&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=genetic'); return(false);">

1237risk assessment</a>

1238 is a consultative service that includes clinical assessment, genetic testing when appropriate, and risk management recommendations delivered in the context of one or more <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44961&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=genetic" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044961&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=genetic'); return(false);">

1239genetic counseling</a>

1240 sessions. Pretest genetic counseling is an important part of the risk assessment process and helps patients understand their genetic testing options and potential outcomes. Posttest genetic counseling helps patients understand their test results, including the medical implications for themselves and their relatives. </p>

1241<p id="_1190" tabindex="-1">

1242The following professional organizations emphasize the importance of genetic counseling in the cancer risk assessment and genetic testing process:</p>

1243<div class="pdq-content-list">

12553</a>

1256,<a href="#cit/section_4.4">

12574</a>

1258]</li>

1260American Society of Human Genetics.[<a href="#cit/section_4.5">

12615</a>

1262,<a href="#cit/section_4.6">

12636</a>

1264]</li>

1266International Society of Nurses in Genetics.[<a href="#cit/section_4.7">

12677</a>

1268,<a href="#cit/section_4.8">

12698</a>

1270]</li>

12739</a>

127511</a>

1292]</li>

1293<li>

1294U.S. Preventive Services Task Force.[<a href="#cit/section_4.17">

129517</a>

1296]</li>

1297</ul>

1298</div>

1299<p id="_1312" tabindex="-1">

1300For a list of organizations that have published clinical practices guidelines related to genetic counseling, risk assessment, genetic testing, and/or management for hereditary breast and gynecologic cancers, see the <a href="/types/breast/hp/breast-ovarian-genetics-pdq#_3079">

1301Indications for hereditary breast and gynecologic cancers genetic testing</a>

1302 section in Genetics of Breast and Gynecologic Cancers. </p>

1303<p id="_321" tabindex="-1">

1304Genetic counseling informs the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=460140&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=genetic" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000460140&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=genetic'); return(false);">

1305consultand</a>

1306 about potential cancer risks and the benefits and limitations of genetic testing and offers an opportunity to consider the potential medical, psychological, familial, and social implications of genetic information.[<a href="#cit/section_4.9">

13079</a>

1308,<a href="#cit/section_4.18">

130918</a>

1310] Descriptions of genetic counseling and the specialized practice of cancer risk assessment counseling are detailed below.</p>

1311<section id="_322">

1312<h3 id="_322_toc">

1313Genetic Counseling</h3>

1314<p id="_1526" tabindex="-1">

1315Genetic counseling has been defined by the National Society of Genetic Counselors as the process of helping people understand and adapt to the medical, psychological, and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=460148&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=genetic" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000460148&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=genetic'); return(false);">

1316familial</a>

1317 implications of genetic contributions to disease, including the following:[<a href="#cit/section_4.9">

13189</a>

1319]</p>

1320<div class="pdq-content-list">

1321<ul id="_1527">

1322<li>

1323How inherited diseases and conditions might affect them or their families.</li>

1324<li>

1325How family and medical histories may impact the chance of disease occurrence or recurrence.</li>

1326<li>

1327Which genetic tests may or may not be right for them, and what those tests may or may not tell.</li>

1328<li>

1329How to make the most informed choices about health care conditions.</li>

1330</ul>

1331</div>

1332<p id="_1540" tabindex="-1">

1333Traditionally, genetic counseling services have been delivered using individualized in-person appointments. However, other methodologies have been implemented, including group sessions, telephone counseling, and online genetic counseling using remote videoconferencing, which is often referred to as <em>

1334telegenetics</em>

1335. For more information, see the <a href="/about-cancer/causes-prevention/genetics/risk-assessment-pdq#_1489">

1336Modalities of genetic counseling</a>

1337 section.</p>

1338<p id="_152" tabindex="-1">

1339Central to the philosophy and practice of genetic counseling are the principles of

1340voluntary utilization of services, informed decision making, attention to

1341psychosocial and affective dimensions of coping with genetic risk, and

1342protection of patient confidentiality and privacy. This is facilitated through a combination of

1343rapport building and information gathering; establishing or verifying

1344diagnoses; risk assessment and calculation of quantitative

1345occurrence/recurrence risks; education and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44677&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=genetic" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044677&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=genetic'); return(false);">

1346informed consent</a>

1347 processes;

1348psychosocial assessment, support, and counseling appropriate to a family&#8217;s

1349culture and ethnicity; and other relevant background characteristics.[<a href="#cit/section_4.19">

135019</a>

1351,<a href="#cit/section_4.20">

135220</a>

1353] The psychosocial assessment is especially important in the genetic counseling process because individuals most vulnerable to adverse effects of genetic information may include those who have had difficulty dealing with stressful life events in the past.[<a href="#cit/section_4.21">

135421</a>

1355] Variables that may influence psychosocial adjustment to genetic information include individual and familial factors; cultural factors; and health system factors such as the type of test, disease status, and risk information.[<a href="#cit/section_4.21">

135621</a>

1357] Findings from a psychosocial assessment can be used to help guide the direction of the counseling session.[<a href="#cit/section_4.10">

135810</a>

1359] An important objective of genetic counseling is to provide an opportunity for shared decision making when the medical benefits of one course of action are not demonstrated to be superior to another. The relationship between the availability of effective medical treatment for <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=460132&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=genetic" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000460132&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=genetic'); return(false);">

1360carriers</a>

1361 of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=783960&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=genetic" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000783960&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=genetic'); return(false);">

1362pathogenic variants</a>

1363 and the clinical validity of a given test affects the degree to which personal choice or physician recommendation is supported in counseling at-risk individuals.[<a href="#cit/section_4.22">

136422</a>

1365] Uptake of genetic counseling services among those referred varies based on the cancer syndrome and the clinical setting. Efforts to decrease barriers to service utilization are ongoing (e.g., the use of a patient navigator or an oncology clinic&#8211;based genetic counselor may increase utilization of these services).[<a href="#cit/section_4.23">

136623</a>

1367-<a href="#cit/section_4.25">

136825</a>

1369] Readers

1370interested in the nature and history of genetic counseling are referred to a

1371number of comprehensive reviews.[<a href="#cit/section_4.26">

137226</a>

1373-<a href="#cit/section_4.31">

137431</a>

1375]</p>

1376</section>

1377<section id="_323">

1378<h3 id="_323_toc">

1379Pretest Genetic Education and Counseling Outcomes</h3>

1380<p id="_324" tabindex="-1">

1381Cancer risk assessment counseling has emerged as a specialized practice that requires knowledge of genetics, oncology, and individual and family counseling skills that may be provided by health care providers with this interdisciplinary training.[<a href="#cit/section_4.32">

138232</a>

1383] Some centers providing cancer risk assessment services involve a multidisciplinary team, which may include a genetic counselor; a genetics advanced practice nurse; a medical geneticist or a physician, such as an oncologist, surgeon, or internist; and a mental health professional. </p>

1384</section>
